  <span id="freeText16289426796470167834" style="display:none">Full of enchantment and wonder, this <i>East of the Sun, West of the Moon</i> retelling was exactly the kind of fantasy story I've been missing in my life lately. The original story is very akin to <i>Beauty and the Beast</i>, but this particular retelling allows for more trolls, more white bears, more questing...more everything. I can't believe I never knew this book existed, not until I saw people talking about <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/31822495-west" rel="nofollow noopener">West</a>
</i>. I have seriously been missing out because Rose is kind of the perfect heroine: fierce and determined to set out and do the things that everyone keeps telling her she can't or mustn't, not to <i>spite</i> them but because she has to right a wrong and nothing is going to stop her, especially busy bodies and naysayers. I loved this book, absolutely loved it, and I'm so glad I already have <i>West </i>downloaded from the library.</span>

<div id="review_2483743203" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2483743203" />
    <a title="nuin giliath" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/69607555-nuin-giliath"><img alt="nuin giliath" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1595720802p2/69607555.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2483743203?book_show_action=true">Jan 02, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="nuin giliath" class="user" itemprop="url" name="nuin giliath" href="/user/show/69607555-nuin-giliath">nuin giliath</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/69607555-nuin-giliath?shelf=magic">magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/69607555-nuin-giliath?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/69607555-nuin-giliath?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/69607555-nuin-giliath?shelf=retellings">retellings</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/69607555-nuin-giliath?shelf=fairy-tale">fairy-tale</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2483743203" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6605597962176840506"><b>*Very mild spoilers are present throughout the review*</b><br/><br/>First book completed in 2020! 🎉<br/><br/>I admit that I am not terribly familiar with the tale that this was based on - <i>East of the Sun and West of the Moon</i>. All I knew at the start was that there would be a white bear who was under some sort of enchantment and a girl who goes with him to a magical home. Needless to say, I was rather surprised to discover that this only described part of the full story. While I can't say how close to the source materia</span>
  <span id="freeText6605597962176840506" style="display:none"><b>*Very mild spoilers are present throughout the review*</b><br /><br />First book completed in 2020! 🎉<br /><br />I admit that I am not terribly familiar with the tale that this was based on - <i>East of the Sun and West of the Moon</i>. All I knew at the start was that there would be a white bear who was under some sort of enchantment and a girl who goes with him to a magical home. Needless to say, I was rather surprised to discover that this only described part of the full story. While I can't say how close to the source material this retelling is, I did find this to be an incredible and lovely fairy tale on its own.<br /><br />The main character, Rose, was a wonderful heroine as she was brave and resilient. When situations seemed impossible or hopeless, she always found a way to persevere. Her friendship with the white bear and how she came to care for him was so sweet. I also enjoyed reading about her early experiences with her family - the circumstances surrounding her birth, her mother's superstitions, the way her father cared for her, and her closeness with her brother. That really helped to develop Rose's character and provided a fascinating look into her life prior to leaving with the white bear.<br /><br />I somewhat expected this to take place in a fantasy world, but instead this was a blend of real-world history with hidden magical realms and it ended up working so much better than I would have anticipated. In the author's note, she commented about the research she did for this story and it shows. While I may not be knowledgeable in sailing, sewing, or some of the cultures featured (Norwegian, Inuit), everything presented here seemed realistic and natural.<br /><br />One of the things I loved most about this book was the various narrators. Each chapter was told in the POV of a different character. I was quite impressed with how the author gave each one a unique voice and perspective. I also commend the narrators of the audiobook that I listened to because they did a fantastic job as well.<br /><br />Not only were the chapters often short, but the text was so well written that I found myself devouring page and page, never wanting to stop. Occasionally, some of the text got bogged down with unnecessary details - particularly passages regarding Rose's routine at the castle or her voyage in the <i>knorr</i>. In my opinion, the third part of the story dragged the most as it focused primarily on Rose traveling and the hardships she endured along the way.<br /><br />Outside of that, there were two other aspects that I wish had been stronger. First, the romance was extremely subtle. I appreciated the slow development of the friendship and I completely bought the concept that these two characters cared deeply for each other. But love? Eh… not so much. I also thought the conflict was resolved too easily (and even seemed a bit far-fetched.) I mean, it did align with how a traditional fairy tale might end, but I guess I was hoping for something a bit more spectacular given the long journey that it took to reach the end.<br /><br />Despite these issues, I maintain that this was still a beautiful story and a new favorite of mine. I would definitely recommend this to fans of fairy tales - whether traditional or retellings.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6605597962176840506" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9804517?shelf=russian-vibes">russian-vibes</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9804517?shelf=girlpower">girlpower</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9804517?shelf=seriously-underrated">seriously-underrated</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2370155018" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11737550712245331902">Let me start off by admitting I've never actually read the original fairytale this retelling is based off of, something I intend to remedy soon (I hope). <br/><br/>Going into this book I was thinking it was the same retelling I had DNFed years ago & was willing to give it another chance. I'm so glad I wanted to give it a "second chance" because in doing so I discovered a book I <i>hadn't</i> actually tried before, and it turned out to be a really good one besides! It was a lucky surprise :D My rating for this on</span>
  <span id="freeText11737550712245331902" style="display:none">Let me start off by admitting I've never actually read the original fairytale this retelling is based off of, something I intend to remedy soon (I hope). <br /><br />Going into this book I was thinking it was the same retelling I had DNFed years ago &amp; was willing to give it another chance. I'm so glad I wanted to give it a "second chance" because in doing so I discovered a book I <i>hadn't</i> actually tried before, and it turned out to be a really good one besides! It was a lucky surprise :D My rating for this one is a nice plump <b>4.75 stars</b><br /><br />The layout of this tale is told via multiple PoVs, which in most cases drives me nuts (I prefer 2 max, though I can suffer 3), but in this book's case it actually worked out pretty well. I mean obviously at times I was annoyed to switch away when things were getting dramatic, but over all the extra perspectives lent more depth to the world building and plot. And each on stood out as a separate individual instead of sounding all alike. <br /><br />There's so many aspects of this story that I just absolutely loved!! From the time period (1500s in Norway), the Norse mythology woven in here and there, the progress of mapping unexplored places, compasses &amp; other navigational equipment, looms &amp; weaving, the survival techniques of the Inuit peoples of Greenland blew my mind!! They're so resourceful and adaptable. I loved reading about all that. And then of course the fairytale influences that the book is based off of, as well as the wide cast of characters we meet along the way. Then to top it all off with an engaging plot full of personal growth, magic &amp; mystery, a journey of epic proportions driven by loyalty, courage, and love. It was just a beautiful written epic, and with all those intricate details giving the world of this story so much realism and layers, I couldn't get enough of it! Obviously, I read it in one sitting it was that riveting.<br /><br />Normally with fantasy I prefer it to be set in a fantastical, made up world. But there are the odd few books, this one especially, that I do really enjoy being set in our real world past. You get all the flavors of fantasy, but you also get all this great culture and history to lend the story age and diversity (especially in the hands of such a skilled writer). We get so many tidbits of all of this throughout the tale, that I just wanted more info on so many different little things. Who doesn't love a book that entertains, as well as teaches you something? Or at least piques your interest into learning more about something on the side?<br /><br />As I'm not familiar with the original fairytale (yet), I can't say how closely this retelling follows that story's layout, but I did see essences of other fairytales, which I of course loved. For instance, Rose and the white bear (and his curse) is very similar to the <i>Beauty and the Beast</i> storyline, and in particular reminded me of Meagan Spooner's <i>Hunted</i> because of the long journey through wilderness, though <i>East</i> is sooooo much better on all counts. Then we also have Rose's father out searching for her, just like Belle's father did, except he was a mapmaker instead of a woodcutter/tinker. Love the similarities though. <br /><br />This book also reminded me of Rumplestiltskin with all the talk of weaving, and especially when Rose weaves cloth of gold to make a dress! And then of course near the end when Rose <i>finally</i> wears that lovely moon dress, as well as borrowed slippers, gloves, and a mask, I had strong <i>Cinderella</i> vibes. It was all so magical and wonderful!! :D <br /><br />The range of cast covered the entire scale of personality types. And so many among them I loved! Just for themselves, and also for the help they gave Rose along the way: Sofi and her daughter Estelle for taking her in, Serge (Sofi's brother) for locating a ship for her, Gest and Goren for being friendly &amp; kind when Thor was certainly wasn't, even Thor with his drunken moods, Malmo the Inuit Shaman for her wisdom &amp; companionship &amp; guiding Rose to near journey's end, Neddy &amp; Rose's father for their love and dedication to bringing her safely back home, Soren for his kindness and generosity to Rose's family and to complete strangers, and of course dear sweet innocent Tuki (I loved him instantly!). There's just so many good people in this! <br /><br />And of course Rose is a <i>truly</i> strong and courageous female lead, one of the best I've read about in a long time. <b>THIS</b> is how you write one!! Not obnoxious &amp; egotistical to misinterpret strength, like so many authors are doing right now. Brave, loyal, caring, and doing what needs to be done because no one else will. THAT'S what makes a strong character. And Ms. Pattou did it all marvelously!! Rose is one of my new all-time favorite heroines &lt;3 You love her from the beginning and root for her till the very last page. And of course, I can't forget to give a shout out to the white bear himself. That gentle, lonely soul who you just wanted to hug and read to to keep the darkness away. <br /><br />The <i>only</i> problem with this book was the handful of slow points here and there, but particularly in the beginning stages of the "journey" portion of it (at about the halfway point). BUT there's no such thing as a journey that is entertainment ALL the time. Slow points are expected. All the great journeys have them: <i>Lord of the Rings, Harry Potter and the Deathly Hallows</i>, etc. So I really shouldn't dock any stars from my rating for that, and yet I just don't feel it's <i>quite</i> worth the full 5. So that being said, I'm just going to subtract a <i>teensy</i> little smidge from the rating. <br /><br />But I <b>
  <i>do</i>
</b> highly recommend this for anyone who loves any of the following:<br /> ~Fairytale retellings<br /> ~Stories WITHOUT the trope-ish "insta loves"<br /> ~Mythology &amp; old world culture<br /> ~Epic journeys<br /> ~Kick-ass heroine<br /> ~Great supporting cast<br /> ~Lovable talking bears<br /> ~Character growth &amp; worldbuilding</span>
  <a data-text-id="11737550712245331902" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText10021887243776564068" style="display:none">Why did I read this book? New cover pretty. <br /><br />I'm glad that I stuck around to the end of this one. It is very different than what I usually read, and I'm being generous with my rating because I was extremely bored during a large portion of this book. <br /><br />This dr a g g e d. <br /><br />It was simply too long to hold my attention. <br /><br />I liked the story and the Norwegian mythology associated with it. I liked having multiple perspectives. The POV of the Troll Queen was something that made me want to continue- so that I could figure out why the heck her POV was so important. <br /><br />This is pretty Beauty and the Beast slash Shrek reminiscent for me. Probably because I grew up watching Disney's BatB and Shrek all the time. Still made me laugh, though. <br /><br />One thing that was super interesting about this was the inordinate amount of time it took to get places. Rose traversed the land for an EnTIre YEaR to get to the... North Pole, I guess? The only thing I have continuously worked on for a year is reading Harry Potter in German (still only 114 pages in... started 13 months ago...). <br /><br />The language used in this book was also pretty cool. I'm like 98% sure that all of the non-English names and terms were Norwegian. It was interesting to learn the names for various European locales in Norwegian. <br /><br />The problems experienced in this one are way different than what I usually read. I read almost exclusively YA so most of the conflicts I read about are angst related. It was a breath of fresh air to read something not totally hormonal. Though I do live for the drama. <br /><br />Here's the thing: I simply didn't care about this book. I probably would have enjoyed it more had I read it at age 10 or something. </span>

  <span id="freeText10422911187533983218" style="display:none">Yeah, so honestly. <div id="review_70352535" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/70352535" />
    <a title="Steph Su" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2010935-steph-su"><img alt="Steph Su" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1504243050p2/2010935.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/70352535?book_show_action=true">Sep 07, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Steph Su" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Steph Su" href="/user/show/2010935-steph-su">Steph Su</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2010935-steph-su?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2010935-steph-su?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2010935-steph-su?shelf=best-of-11">best-of-11</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2010935-steph-su?shelf=writing-learn">writing-learn</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer70352535" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13546780838583689297">EAST is the tale of Rose, who sacrifices her freedom to save her sister, grows to care for the cursed white bear who is her “captor,” unwittingly betrays him, then goes beyond the ends of the earth to make things right. It’s a classic folktale that never fails to move me, but Edith Pattou’s retelling of “East of the Sun, West of the Moon” went above and beyond, astounding me with its magical rendering of a traditional story and simple literary elements.<br/><br/>EAST is not extraordinarily sophisticated i</span>
  <span id="freeText13546780838583689297" style="display:none">EAST is the tale of Rose, who sacrifices her freedom to save her sister, grows to care for the cursed white bear who is her “captor,” unwittingly betrays him, then goes beyond the ends of the earth to make things right. It’s a classic folktale that never fails to move me, but Edith Pattou’s retelling of “East of the Sun, West of the Moon” went above and beyond, astounding me with its magical rendering of a traditional story and simple literary elements.<br /><br />EAST is not extraordinarily sophisticated in writing style: narration alters between several different voices, and none of them particularly stand out as individual examples of great literariness. However, the magic of EAST lies in how these common elements—straightforward prose, a retelling—fit together. The multiple narrators adds a unique rhythm and scope to the story that makes the whole so much more than the sum of its parts. <br /><br />Edith Pattou sets EAST in historical Europe, and the story traverses lands, cultures, seas, and languages for an astonishing and engrossing read. This is the second retelling of “East of the Sun, West of the Moon” that I’ve had the pleasure of reading, and I’m astonished at the different directions in which each author took this folktale. I’m no history buff, but I was mesmerized by Edith Pattou’s description of the various people that Rose meets on her journey, by the variety of people and cultures that existed over great distances at the same time.<br /><br />Words fail me when I try to describe an extraordinary book; indeed, there is no part of this book that was not amazing, and thus there is no part that I can describe well. There is a reason I still see this book in bookstores: it has the rare lasting power that only the most accomplished of fantasy reads possess.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13546780838583689297" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_25089913" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/25089913" />
    <a title="Mary-Beth" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/119580-mary-beth"><img alt="Mary-Beth" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1341960385p2/119580.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/25089913?book_show_action=true">Jun 21, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mary-Beth" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mary-Beth" href="/user/show/119580-mary-beth">Mary-Beth</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780152045630" href="/book/show/981170.East">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/119580-mary-beth?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/119580-mary-beth?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/119580-mary-beth?shelf=fairy-tales">fairy-tales</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer25089913" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8546942051612881465">For a re-telling this was very good. In many ways, other than just expanding on the original, this version seemed to try to add some realism to the tale. Fortunately it wasn't realism at the cost of magic. There was still plenty of magic. Don't look for anything staggeringly innovative here and the writing isn't perfect, but this is very readable.<br/><br/>The novel delineated an ordinary world from a magical world by making Rose's home life somewhat more mundane as well as keeping from her many of the ma</span>
  <span id="freeText8546942051612881465" style="display:none">For a re-telling this was very good. In many ways, other than just expanding on the original, this version seemed to try to add some realism to the tale. Fortunately it wasn't realism at the cost of magic. There was still plenty of magic. Don't look for anything staggeringly innovative here and the writing isn't perfect, but this is very readable.<br /><br />The novel delineated an ordinary world from a magical world by making Rose's home life somewhat more mundane as well as keeping from her many of the magical resources she receives in the fairy tale. This also worked to make Rose's journey seem much more full of hardships than is the shorter version.<br /><br />Anyway, I'm making it sound somewhat boring when it wasn't. I liked the characters and enjoyed many of the additions to the story which the author added, such as the fact that the bear had a great difficulty speaking, Rose's love of weaving, her father's fascination with map-making and her mother's superstitions and a great deal of description about the trolls.<br /><br />There are many memorable and interesting original characters here, not to mention the fact that the author manages to remove much of the stigma of the curious woman and the jealous mother that existed in the original by making the characters much more complex and forgiving. </span>
  <a data-text-id="8546942051612881465" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText10119779745979039735" style="display:none">Since I read this back when I was first becoming interested in YA, I was worried that a second reading would prove to be less enjoyable.   function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('x/QCNfhd9Hj+1zvV5hOBiHpNCu0KclGCn6hqZpmyAXblx5zmBLudBSH+7LSZGrQc89HMVyzGjwlMct3z7FKzUQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('xlduwzqvmf126bdcJPtyUY4oH84vVYvhDw65x6m4cJ7kZPAQxknwgKnAYD1b8kfFB7TZdAnhVWrc1A5S3FjCuQ==')})
  }
